<p><b>Pennsylvania</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">j</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Pennsylvania.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/En-us-Pennsylvania.ogg" title="En-us-Pennsylvania.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span> (<a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_German_language" title="Pennsylvania German language">Pennsylvania German</a>: <i>Pennsylvaani</i> or <i>Pennsilfaani</i>), officially the <b>Commonwealth of Pennsylvania</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">northeastern</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_States" title="Mid-Atlantic States">Mid-Atlantic</a> regions of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> run through its middle. The <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">Commonwealth</a> borders <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a> to the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories">Canadian</a> province of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> to the east.</p>
<p>Pennsylvania is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">33rd-largest</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">6th-most populous</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population density">9th-most densely populated</a> of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_and_territories_of_the_United_States" title="List of states and territories of the United States">50 United States</a>. The state's five most populous cities are <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> (1,560,297), <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> (305,801), <a href="/wiki/Allentown,_Pennsylvania" title="Allentown, Pennsylvania">Allentown</a> (118,577), <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">Erie</a> (100,671), and <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Pennsylvania" title="Reading, Pennsylvania">Reading</a> (89,893). The state capital, and its ninth-largest city, is <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Harrisburg, Pennsylvania">Harrisburg</a>. Pennsylvania has 140 miles (225 km) of shoreline along <a href="/wiki/Erie_Triangle" title="Erie Triangle">Lake Erie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware</a> Estuary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coastalmanagement.noaa.gov_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coastalmanagement.noaa.gov-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state is one of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">13 original founding states</a> of the United States; it came into being in 1681 as a result of a royal land grant to <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a>, the son of the state's namesake. Part of Pennsylvania (along the Delaware River), together with the present State of Delaware, had earlier been organized as the Colony of New Sweden. It was the second state to ratify the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>, on December 12, 1787. <a href="/wiki/Independence_Hall" title="Independence Hall">Independence Hall</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a> and United States Constitution were drafted, is located in the state's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Pennsylvania" title="List of cities in Pennsylvania">largest city</a> of Philadelphia. During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a> was fought in the <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Pennsylvania" title="South Central Pennsylvania">south central</a> region of the state. <a href="/wiki/Valley_Forge_National_Historical_Park" title="Valley Forge National Historical Park">Valley Forge</a> near Philadelphia was <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">General Washington</a>'s headquarters during the bitter winter of 1777–78.</p>
<p></p>

</div>
<p>Pennsylvania is 170 miles (274 km) north to south and 283 miles (455 km) east to west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pageo_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-pageo-9">[9]</a></sup> Of a total 46,055 square miles (119,282 km<sup>2</sup>), 44,817 square miles (116,075 km<sup>2</sup>) are land, 490 square miles (1,269 km<sup>2</sup>) are inland waters, and 749 square miles (1,940 km<sup>2</sup>) are waters in Lake Erie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statabs_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-statabs-10">[10]</a></sup> It is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_area" title="List of U.S. states by area">33rd-largest state</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Pennsylvania has 51 miles (82 km)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cr.nps.gov_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cr.nps.gov-12">[12]</a></sup> of coastline along <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a> and 57 miles (92 km)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coastalmanagement.noaa.gov_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Coastalmanagement.noaa.gov-8">[8]</a></sup> of shoreline along the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware Estuary</a>.</p>
<p>The boundaries of the state are the <a href="/wiki/Mason%E2%80%93Dixon_line" title="Mason–Dixon line">Mason–Dixon line</a> (39° 43' N) to the south, the <a href="/wiki/Twelve-Mile_Circle" title="Twelve-Mile Circle">Twelve-Mile Circle</a> on the Pennsylvania-Delaware border, the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a> to the east, 80° 31' W to the west and the <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42° N</a> to the north, with the exception of a short segment on the western end, where a triangle extends north to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>.</p>
<p>Cities include <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Pennsylvania" title="Reading, Pennsylvania">Reading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon,_Pennsylvania" title="Lebanon, Pennsylvania">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_Pennsylvania" title="Lancaster, Pennsylvania">Lancaster</a> in the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> in the southwest, the tri-cities of <a href="/wiki/Allentown,_Pennsylvania" title="Allentown, Pennsylvania">Allentown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem,_Pennsylvania" title="Bethlehem, Pennsylvania">Bethlehem</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Easton,_Pennsylvania" title="Easton, Pennsylvania">Easton</a> in the central east (known as the <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley" title="Lehigh Valley">Lehigh Valley</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Pennsylvania" title="Northeastern Pennsylvania">northeast</a> includes the former anthracite coal mining communities of <a href="/wiki/Scranton,_Pennsylvania" title="Scranton, Pennsylvania">Scranton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilkes-Barre,_Pennsylvania" title="Wilkes-Barre, Pennsylvania">Wilkes-Barre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittston,_Pennsylvania" title="Pittston, Pennsylvania">Pittston City</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greater_Pittston" title="Greater Pittston">Greater Pittston</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Hazleton,_Pennsylvania" title="Hazleton, Pennsylvania">Hazleton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">Erie</a> is located in the northwest. <a href="/wiki/Williamsport,_Pennsylvania" title="Williamsport, Pennsylvania">Williamsport</a> serves as the commonwealth's north-central region, with <a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">York</a> and the state capital Harrisburg on the <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_River" title="Susquehanna River">Susquehanna River</a> in the east-central region of the Commonwealth and Altoona and Johnstown in the west-central region.</p>
<p>The state has 5 regions, namely the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Plateau" title="Allegheny Plateau">Allegheny Plateau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ridge-and-Valley_Appalachians" title="Ridge-and-Valley Appalachians">Ridge and Valley</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coastal_Plain" title="Atlantic Coastal Plain">Atlantic Coastal Plain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)" title="Piedmont (United States)">Piedmont</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Plain" title="Erie Plain">Erie Plain</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_States">Adjacent States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Adjacent States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> (North)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario, Canada</a> (Northwest)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> (South)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> (Southeast)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a> (Southwest)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> (East)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> (West)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PA_koppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="1305" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/PA_koppen.svg/220px-PA_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/PA_koppen.svg/330px-PA_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/PA_koppen.svg/440px-PA_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PA_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Köppen climate types of Pennsylvania</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3149" data-file-width="4608" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_%281%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_%281%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_%281%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Nicholas_T_-_Endless_Mountains_Landscape_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Autumn in North Branch Township, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Wyoming County, Pennsylvania">Wyoming County, Pennsylvania</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Pennsylvania" title="Climate of Pennsylvania">Climate of Pennsylvania</a></div>
<p>Pennsylvania's diverse topography also produces a variety of climates, though the entire state experiences cold winters and humid summers. Straddling two major zones, the majority of the state, with the exception of the southeastern corner, has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfa</i>). The largest city, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, has some characteristics of the <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (Köppen <i>Cfa</i>) that covers much of <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> to the south.</p>
<p>Moving toward the mountainous interior of the state, the winter climate becomes colder, the number of cloudy days increase, and snowfall amounts are greater. Western areas of the state, particularly locations near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>, can receive over 100 inches (250 cm) of snowfall annually, and the entire state receives plentiful precipitation throughout the year. The state may be subject to severe weather from spring through summer into fall. Tornadoes occur annually in the state, sometimes in large numbers, such as 30 recorded tornadoes in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Pennsylvania" title="History of Pennsylvania">History of Pennsylvania</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">Province of Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pennsylvania_firsts" title="List of Pennsylvania firsts">List of Pennsylvania firsts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Pennsylvania" title="List of people from Pennsylvania">List of people from Pennsylvania</a></div>
<p>Long before the Commonwealth was visited and later settled by Europeans, the area was home to subgroups of the <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Delaware</a> (also known as Lenni Lenape), <a href="/wiki/Susquehannock" title="Susquehannock">Susquehannock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eriez" title="Eriez">Eriez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a>, and still other <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a> Nations of uncertain designation. The Tuscarora Nation took up temporary residence in the central portion of Pennsylvania ca. 1715–55.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="17th_century">17th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 17th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="674" data-file-width="1084" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png/200px-Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png/300px-Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png/400px-Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Darlington_map_of_Pennsylvania_1680.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British map of Pennsylvania from 1680 (from the <a href="/wiki/Darlington_Collection" title="Darlington Collection">Darlington Collection</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Both the <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">Dutch</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Company" title="Virginia Company">English</a> claimed both sides of the Delaware River as part of their colonial lands in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Zandt_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Zandt-22">[22]</a></sup> The Dutch were the first to take possession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van_Zandt_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Van_Zandt-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>By June 3, 1631, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> had begun settling the <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Peninsula" title="Delmarva Peninsula">Delmarva Peninsula</a> by establishing the <a href="/wiki/Zwaanendael_Colony" title="Zwaanendael Colony">Zwaanendael Colony</a> on the site of present-day <a href="/wiki/Lewes,_Delaware" title="Lewes, Delaware">Lewes, Delaware</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1638, Sweden established the <a href="/wiki/New_Sweden" title="New Sweden">New Sweden Colony</a>, in the region of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Christina" title="Fort Christina">Fort Christina</a>, on the site of present-day <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">Wilmington, Delaware</a>. New Sweden claimed and, for the most part, controlled the lower Delaware River region (parts of present-day Delaware, New Jersey, and Pennsylvania) but settled few colonists there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="799" data-file-width="944" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg/220px-Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg/330px-Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg/440px-Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edward_Hicks_-_Penn%27s_Treaty.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Penn's Treaty with the Indians</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hicks" title="Edward Hicks">Edward Hicks</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On March 12, 1664, <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">King Charles II of England</a> gave <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James, Duke of York</a> a grant that incorporated all lands included in the original Virginia Company of Plymouth Grant plus other lands. This grant was in conflict with the Dutch claim for <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a>, which included parts of today's Pennsylvania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 24, 1664, the Duke of York sold the portion of his large grant that included present-day <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> to <a href="/wiki/John_Berkeley,_1st_Baron_Berkeley_of_Stratton" title="John Berkeley, 1st Baron Berkeley of Stratton">John Berkeley</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Carteret" title="George Carteret">George Carteret</a> for a proprietary colony. The land was not yet in British possession, but the sale boxed in the portion of New Netherland on the West side of the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a>. The British conquest of New Netherland began on August 29, 1664, when <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> was coerced to surrender while facing cannons on British ships in New York Harbor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> This conquest continued, and was completed in October 1664, when the British captured <a href="/wiki/Fort_Casimir" title="Fort Casimir">Fort Casimir</a> in what today is <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Delaware" title="New Castle, Delaware">New Castle, Delaware</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Dickinson_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="300" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/John_Dickinson_portrait.jpg/170px-John_Dickinson_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/John_Dickinson_portrait.jpg/255px-John_Dickinson_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/John_Dickinson_portrait.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Dickinson_portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Dickinson_(delegate)" title="John Dickinson (delegate)">John Dickinson</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_of_Breda" title="Peace of Breda">Peace of Breda</a> between England, France and the Netherlands confirmed the English conquest on July 21, 1667,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> although there were temporary reversions.</p>
<p>On September 12, 1672, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Third Anglo-Dutch War">Third Anglo-Dutch War</a>, the Dutch re-conquered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Colony" title="New York Colony">New York Colony</a>/<a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a>, the Dutch established three County Courts which went on to become original Counties in present-day <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> and Pennsylvania. The one that later transferred to Pennsylvania was Upland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> This was partially reversed on February 9, 1674, when the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Westminster_(1674)" title="Treaty of Westminster (1674)">Treaty of Westminster</a> ended the Third Anglo-Dutch War, and reverted all political situations to the <i>status quo ante bellum</i>. The British retained the Dutch Counties with their Dutch names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> By June 11, 1674, New York reasserted control over the outlying colonies, including Upland, but the names started to be changed to British names by November 11, 1674.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Upland was partitioned on November 12, 1674, producing the general outline of the current border between Pennsylvania and Delaware.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 28, 1681, Charles II granted a land charter<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a> to repay a debt of £16,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> (around £2,100,000 in 2008, adjusting for retail inflation)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> owed to William's father, <a href="/wiki/William_Penn_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="William Penn (Royal Navy officer)">Admiral William Penn</a>. This was one of the largest land grants to an individual in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quapoly_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-quapoly-38">[38]</a></sup> The King named it Pennsylvania (literally "Penn's Woods") in honor of the Admiral. Penn, the son, who wanted it to be called New Wales, and then Sylvania (from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>silva</i>: "forest, woods"), was embarrassed at the change, fearing that people would think he had named it after himself, but King Charles would not rename the grant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Penn established a government with two innovations that were much copied in the New World: the <a href="/wiki/County_commission" title="County commission">county commission</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religious conviction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quapoly_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-quapoly-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America,_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6442" data-file-width="7399" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America%2C_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png/220px-A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America%2C_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America%2C_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png/330px-A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America%2C_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America%2C_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png/440px-A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America%2C_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_mapp_of_ye_improved_part_of_Pensilvania_in_America,_divided_into_countyes_townships_and_lotts.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A mapp of ye improved part of Pensilvania in America, divided into countyes townships and lotts</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>What had been Upland on what became the Pennsylvania side of the Pennsylvania-<a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> Border was renamed as <a href="/wiki/Chester_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester County, Pennsylvania">Chester County</a> when Pennsylvania instituted their colonial governments on March 4, 1681.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Quakers" title="Quakers">Quaker</a> leader <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a> had signed a peace treaty with <a href="/wiki/Tamanend" title="Tamanend">Tammany</a>, leader of the Delaware tribe, beginning a long period of friendly relations between the Quakers and the Indians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Additional treaties between Quakers and other tribes followed. The <a href="/wiki/Penn_Treaty_Park" title="Penn Treaty Park">treaty</a> of William Penn was never violated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 1730 and when it was shut down by Parliament with the Currency Act of 1764, the Pennsylvania Colony made its own paper money to account for the shortage of actual gold and silver. The paper money was called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Scrip" title="Colonial Scrip">Colonial Scrip</a>. The Colony issued "bills of credit", which were as good as gold or silver coins because of their legal tender status. Since they were issued by the government and not a banking institution, it was an interest-free proposition, largely defraying the expense of the government and therefore taxation of the people. It also promoted general employment and prosperity, since the Government used discretion and did not issue too much to inflate the currency. <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a> had a hand in creating this currency, of which he said its utility was never to be disputed, and it also met with the "cautious approval" of <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/James_Smith_(frontiersman)" title="James Smith (frontiersman)">James Smith</a> wrote that in 1763, "the Indians again commenced hostilities, and were busily engaged in killing and scalping the frontier inhabitants in various parts of Pennsylvania." Further, "This state was then a Quaker government, and at the first of this war the frontiers received no assistance from the state."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The ensuing hostilities became known as <a href="/wiki/Pontiac%27s_War" title="Pontiac's War">Pontiac's War</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="455" data-file-width="674" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg/220px-PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg/330px-PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg/440px-PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PhiladelphiaPresidentsHouse.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/President%27s_House_(Philadelphia)" title="President's House (Philadelphia)">President's House (Philadelphia)</a>. The Masters-Penn mansion housed Pennsylvania's governor in the early 1770s. It later served as the presidential mansion of <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">John Adams</a>, 1790–1800, while Philadelphia was the temporary national capital.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Act_Congress" title="Stamp Act Congress">Stamp Act Congress</a> of 1765, Delegate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Dickinson_(delegate)" title="John Dickinson (delegate)">John Dickinson</a> of <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> wrote the <i><a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Rights_and_Grievances" title="Declaration of Rights and Grievances">Declaration of Rights and Grievances</a></i>. The Congress was the first meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>, called at the request of the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> Assembly, but only nine colonies sent delegates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Dickinson then wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Letters_from_a_Farmer_in_Pennsylvania" title="Letters from a Farmer in Pennsylvania">Letters from a Farmer in Pennsylvania, To the Inhabitants of the British Colonies</a></i>, which were published in the Pennsylvania Chronicle between December 2, 1767, and February 15, 1768.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States" title="Founding Fathers of the United States">Founding Fathers of the United States</a> convened in Philadelphia in 1774, 12 colonies sent representatives to the <a href="/wiki/First_Continental_Congress" title="First Continental Congress">First Continental Congress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">Second Continental Congress</a>, which also met in Philadelphia (in May 1775), drew up and signed the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> in Philadelphia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> but when that city was captured by the British, the Continental Congress escaped westward, meeting at the <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_Pennsylvania" title="Lancaster, Pennsylvania">Lancaster</a> courthouse on Saturday, September 27, 1777, and then to <a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">York</a>. There they and its primary author, John Dickinson, drew up the <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">Articles of Confederation</a> that formed 13 independent colonies into a new nation. Later, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution</a> was written, and Philadelphia was once again chosen to be cradle to the new American Nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The Constitution was drafted and signed at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_House" title="Pennsylvania State House">Pennsylvania State House</a>, now known as Independence Hall, and the same building where the Declaration of Independence was signed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pennsylvania became the first large state, and the second state to ratify the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Constitution" title="U.S. Constitution">U.S. Constitution</a> on December 12, 1787,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> five days after <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> became the first. At the time it was the most ethically and religiously diverse of the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>. Because One-third of Pennsylvania’s population spoke German, the Constitution was presented in German to include those citizens in the discussion. Reverend <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Muhlenberg" title="Frederick Muhlenberg">Frederick Muhlenberg</a> acted as the chairman of the state's ratifying convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dickinson_College" title="Dickinson College">Dickinson College</a> of <a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Pennsylvania" title="Carlisle, Pennsylvania">Carlisle</a> was the first college founded in the United States. Established in 1773, the college was ratified five days after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> on September 9, 1783. The school was founded by <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Rush" title="Benjamin Rush">Benjamin Rush</a> and named after John Dickinson.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HillsCapitol.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="158" data-file-width="200" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/HillsCapitol.jpg" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HillsCapitol.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "Hills Capitol", used from 1821 until it burned down in 1897.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For half a century, the Commonwealth's General Assembly (legislature) met at various places in the general Philadelphia area before starting to meet regularly in Independence Hall in Philadelphia for 63 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup> But it needed a more central location, as for example the <a href="/wiki/Paxton_Boys" title="Paxton Boys">Paxton Boys</a> massacres of 1763 had made the legislature aware. So, in 1799 the General Assembly moved to the <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_Pennsylvania" title="Lancaster, Pennsylvania">Lancaster</a> Courthouse,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup> and finally in 1812 to <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Harrisburg, Pennsylvania">Harrisburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The General Assembly met in the old <a href="/wiki/Dauphin_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Dauphin County, Pennsylvania">Dauphin County</a> Court House until December 1821,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup> when the Federal-style "Hills Capitol" (named for its builder, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hills" title="Stephen Hills">Stephen Hills</a>, a Lancaster architect) was constructed on a hilltop land grant of four acres set aside for a seat of state government by the prescient, entrepreneurial son and namesake of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Harris,_Sr." title="John Harris, Sr.">John Harris, Sr.</a>, a Yorkshire native who had founded a trading post in 1705 and ferry (1733) on the east shore of the Susquehanna River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The Hills Capitol burned down on February 2, 1897, during a heavy snowstorm, presumably because of a faulty <a href="/wiki/Flue" title="Flue">flue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-4"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup> The General Assembly met at Grace Methodist Church on State Street (still standing) until a new capitol could be built. Following an architectural selection contest that many alleged had been "rigged", <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> architect <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ives_Cobb" title="Henry Ives Cobb">Henry Ives Cobb</a> was charged with designing and building a replacement building; however, the legislature had little money to allocate to the project, and a roughly finished, somewhat industrial building (the Cobb Capitol) was completed. The General Assembly refused to occupy the building. Political and popular indignation in 1901 prompted a second contest that was restricted to Pennsylvania architects, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Miller_Huston" title="Joseph Miller Huston">Joseph Miller Huston</a> of Philadelphia was chosen to design the present <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_Capitol" title="Pennsylvania State Capitol">Pennsylvania State Capitol</a> that incorporated Cobb's building into magnificent public work finished and dedicated in 1907.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-5"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_Capitol" title="Pennsylvania State Capitol">new state Capitol</a> drew rave reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-6"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup> Its dome was inspired by the domes of <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a> in Rome and the United States Capitol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-7"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> called it "the most beautiful state Capital in the nation" and said, "It's the handsomest building I ever saw" at the dedication. In 1989, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> praised it as "grand, even awesome at moments, but it is also a working building, accessible to citizens ... a building that connects with the reality of daily life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legiscap_54-8"><a href="#cite_note-legiscap-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/James_Buchanan" title="James Buchanan">James Buchanan</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Franklin_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Franklin County, Pennsylvania">Franklin County</a>, the only bachelor President of the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jimbo_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-jimbo-56">[56]</a></sup> was the only one to be born in Pennsylvania. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a>—the major turning point of the Civil War—took place near <a href="/wiki/Gettysburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Gettysburg, Pennsylvania">Gettysburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> An estimated 350,000 Pennsylvanians served in the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a> forces including 8,600 African American <a href="/wiki/Military_volunteer" title="Military volunteer">military volunteers</a>.</p>
<p>Pennsylvania was also the home of the first commercially drilled oil well. In 1859, near <a href="/wiki/Titusville,_Pennsylvania" title="Titusville, Pennsylvania">Titusville, Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Drake" title="Edwin Drake">Edwin Drake</a> successfully drilled the well, which led to the first major oil boom in United States history.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Relief_Administration" title="Federal Emergency Relief Administration">FERA</a> camp for unemployed women, 1934</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the beginning of the 20th century Pennsylvania's economy was centered around steel production, logging, coal mining, textile production and other forms of industrial manufacturing. A surge in immigration to the U.S. during the late 19th and early 20th centuries provided a steady flow of cheap labor for these industries which often employed children and people who could not speak English.</p>
<p>In 1923 President <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Coolidge" title="Calvin Coolidge">Calvin Coolidge</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_National_Forest" title="Allegheny National Forest">Allegheny National Forest</a> under the authority of the <a href="/wiki/Weeks_Act" title="Weeks Act">Weeks Act</a> of 1911 in the northwest part of the state in Elk, Forest, McKean, and Warren Counties for the purposes of timber production and watershed protection in the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a> basin. The Allegheny is the state's only national forest.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Pennsylvania" title="List of people from Pennsylvania">List of people from Pennsylvania</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Pennsylvania was 12,802,503 on July 1, 2015, a 0.79% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>. In an earlier estimate, the state was 78.8% Non-Hispanic White, 11.4% Black or African American, 0.3% Native American, 3.0% Asian, 0.1% Native Hawaiian and Other Pacific Islander, 1.7% Two or More Races, and 6.1% Hispanic or Latino.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the people residing in Pennsylvania, 74.5% were born in Pennsylvania, 18.4% were born in a different U.S. state, 1.5% were born Puerto Rico, U.S. Island areas, or born abroad to American parent(s), and 5.6% were foreign born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2010 Census, 81.9% of the population was White (79.2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_white" title="Non-Hispanic white">non-Hispanic white</a>), 11.3% was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">Black</a> or African American, 0.3% American Indian and Alaska Native, 2.9% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a>, 1.9% from two or more races. 5.9% of the total population was of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> or Latino origin (they may be of any race).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>

<p>As of 2011, 32.1% of Pennsylvania's population younger than age one were minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pennsylvania's Hispanic population grew by 82.6% between 2000 and 2010, making it one of the largest increases in a state's Hispanic population. The significant growth of the Hispanic population is due to immigration to the state mainly from Puerto Rico, which is a US territory, but to a lesser extent from countries such as the Dominican Republic, Mexico, and various Central and South American nations, as well as from the wave of Hispanics leaving New York and New Jersey for safer and more affordable living. The Asian population swelled by almost 60%, which was fueled by Indian, Vietnamese, and Chinese immigration, as well the many Asian transplants moving to Philadelphia from New York. The rapid growth of this community has given Pennsylvania one of the largest Asian populations in the nation by numerical values. The Black and African American population grew by 13%, which was the largest increase in that population amongst the state's peers (New York, New Jersey, Ohio, Illinois, and Michigan).The White population declined by 0.7%, a trend that is beginning to reverse itself. Twelve other states saw decreases in their White populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The state of Pennsylvania has a high in-migration of blacks and Hispanics from other nearby states, with eastern and south-central portions of the state seeing the bulk of the increases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pasdc.hbg.psu.edu_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-pasdc.hbg.psu.edu-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Pennsylvania is located in <a href="/wiki/Perry_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Perry County, Pennsylvania">Perry County</a>, in the borough of <a href="/wiki/Duncannon,_Pennsylvania" title="Duncannon, Pennsylvania">Duncannon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PennsylvaniaDemography.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="832" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/PennsylvaniaDemography.svg/220px-PennsylvaniaDemography.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/PennsylvaniaDemography.svg/330px-PennsylvaniaDemography.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/PennsylvaniaDemography.svg/440px-PennsylvaniaDemography.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PennsylvaniaDemography.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
State population from 1790 to 2000</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="710" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png/220px-Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png/330px-Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png/440px-Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pennsylvania_population_map_1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pennsylvania's population distribution</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2013, Pennsylvania has an estimated population of 12,773,801, which is an increase of 10,265 from the previous year and an increase of 71,422 since the year 2010. Net <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> to other states resulted in a decrease of 27,718, and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">immigration</a> from other countries resulted in an increase of 127,007. Net migration to the Commonwealth was 98,289. Migration of native Pennsylvanians resulted in a decrease of 100,000 people. From 2008 to 2012, 5.8% of the population was foreign-born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The state has an estimated 2005 poverty rate of 12%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAFacts_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAFacts-70">[70]</a></sup> The state also has the 3rd-highest proportion of elderly (65+) citizens in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAFacts_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-PAFacts-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Foreign born Pennsylvanians are largely from Asia (36.0%), Europe (35.9%), and Latin America (30.6%), with the remainder from Africa (5%), North America (3.1%), and Oceania (0.4%).</p>
<p>The majority of Hispanics in Pennsylvania are of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_American" title="Puerto Rican American">Puerto Rican</a> descent, having one of the largest and fastest-growing Puerto Rican populations in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Most of the remaining Hispanic population is made up of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">Mexicans</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_American" title="Dominican American">Dominicans</a>. Most Hispanics are concentrated in Philadelphia, <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley" title="Lehigh Valley">Lehigh Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Pennsylvania" title="South Central Pennsylvania">South Central Pennsylvania</a>. Pennsylvania's reported population of Hispanics, especially among the Black race, has markedly increased in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-annest_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-annest-73">[73]</a></sup> The Hispanic population is greatest in <a href="/wiki/Hazleton,_Pennsylvania" title="Hazleton, Pennsylvania">Hazleton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allentown,_Pennsylvania" title="Allentown, Pennsylvania">Allentown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Pennsylvania" title="Reading, Pennsylvania">Reading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_Pennsylvania" title="Lancaster, Pennsylvania">Lancaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">York</a>, and around <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>. It is not clear how much of this change reflects a changing population and how much reflects increased willingness to self-identify minority status. As of 2010, it is estimated that about 85% of all Hispanics in Pennsylvania live within a 150-mile (240 km) radius of Philadelphia, with about 20% living within the city itself.</p>
<p>Of the black population, the vast majority in the state are African American, being descendants of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">African slaves brought to the US south</a> during the colonial era. There are also a growing number of blacks of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indian_American" title="West Indian American">West Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="African immigration to the United States">recent African</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Hispanic" title="Black Hispanic">Hispanic</a> origins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Most blacks live in the Philadelphia area, Pittsburgh, and South Central Pennsylvania, among other areas. Whites make-up the majority of Pennsylvania, they are mostly descended from German, Irish, Italian, and English immigrants, among others. Rural portions of South Central Pennsylvania are famous nationwide for its notable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amish_country" title="Amish country">Amish communities</a>. The "<a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Valley" title="Wyoming Valley">Wyoming Valley</a>" or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scranton/Wilkes-Barre_Metropolitan_Area" title="Scranton/Wilkes-Barre Metropolitan Area">Scranton/Wilkes-Barre Metropolitan Area</a> has a large concentration of whites. As a matter of fact, it has the highest percentage of white residents than any other metropolitan area in the U.S. with 96.2% of its population claiming to be white with no Hispanic background.</p>
<p>Pennsylvania's population was reported as 5.9% under 5 and 23.8% under 18, with 15.6% aged 65 or older. Women made up 52% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censusPA_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-censusPA-75">[75]</a></sup> The largest ancestry groups are listed below, expressed as a percentage of total people who responded with a particular ancestry for the 2010 census:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>28.5% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a></li>
<li>18.2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a></li>
<li>12.8% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a></li>
<li>9.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a></li>
<li>8.5% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a></li>
<li>7.2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">Polish</a></li>
<li>4.2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French Canadian</a></li>
</ul>

<p>As of 2010, 90.15% (10,710,239) of Pennsylvania residents age 5 and older spoke English at home as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_language" title="Primary language">primary language</a>, while 4.09% (486,058) spoke Spanish, 0.87% (103,502) German (which includes <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_German_language" title="Pennsylvania German language">Pennsylvania Dutch</a>) and by 0.47% (56,052) Chinese (which includes <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Mandarin</a>) of the population over the age of five. In total, 9.85% (1,170,628) of Pennsylvania's population age 5 and older spoke a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">mother language</a> other than English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_Data_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-MLA_Data-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pennsylvania_German_language">Pennsylvania German language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Pennsylvania German language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_German_language" title="Pennsylvania German language">Pennsylvania German language</a></div>
<p>Pennsylvania German is often—even though misleadingly—called "Pennsylvania Dutch". The term "Dutch", when referring to the language spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch" title="Pennsylvania Dutch">Pennsylvania Dutch people</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_German_language" title="Pennsylvania German language">Pennsylvania German</a>) means "German" or "Teutonic" rather than "Netherlander". Germans, in their own language, call themselves "Deutsch", (Pennsylvania German: "Deitsch") which in English became, misleadingly, "Dutch".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_German_language" title="Pennsylvania German language">Pennsylvania German language</a> is a descendant of German, in the <a href="/wiki/West_Central_German" title="West Central German">West Central German</a> dialect family. It is closest to <a href="/wiki/Palatine_German_language" title="Palatine German language">Palatine German</a>. Pennsylvania German is still very vigorous as a first language among <a href="/wiki/Old_Order_Amish" title="Old Order Amish">Old Order Amish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Order_Mennonite" title="Old Order Mennonite">Old Order Mennonites</a> (principally in the <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Lancaster County, Pennsylvania">Lancaster County area</a>), whereas it is almost extinct as an everyday language outside the <a href="/wiki/Plain_people" title="Plain people">plain communities</a>, though a few words have passed into English usage.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
