<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baughman%27s_Rock_Overlook.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ohiopyle_State_Park" title="Ohiopyle State Park">Ohiopyle State Park</a> timelapse</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All 121 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pennsylvania_state_parks" title="List of Pennsylvania state parks">state parks</a> in Pennsylvania feature free admission.</p>
<p>Pennsylvania offers a number of notable amusement parks, including <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Camel_Beach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Camel Beach (page does not exist)">Camel Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conneaut_Lake_Park" title="Conneaut Lake Park">Conneaut Lake Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dorney_Park_%26_Wildwater_Kingdom" title="Dorney Park &amp; Wildwater Kingdom">Dorney Park &amp; Wildwater Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Wonderland" title="Dutch Wonderland">Dutch Wonderland</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DelGrosso_Amusement_Park" title="DelGrosso Amusement Park">DelGrosso Amusement Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hersheypark" title="Hersheypark">Hersheypark</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idlewild_Park" title="Idlewild Park">Idlewild Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kennywood" title="Kennywood">Kennywood</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knoebels" title="Knoebels">Knoebels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakemont_Park" title="Lakemont Park">Lakemont Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandcastle_Waterpark" title="Sandcastle Waterpark">Sandcastle Waterpark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sesame_Place" title="Sesame Place">Sesame Place</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Wolf_Lodge" title="Great Wolf Lodge">Great Wolf Lodge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waldameer_Park" title="Waldameer Park">Waldameer Park</a>. Pennsylvania also is home to the largest indoor waterpark resort on the East Coast, <a href="/wiki/Splash_Lagoon" title="Splash Lagoon">Splash Lagoon</a> in Erie.</p>
<p>There are also notable music festivals that take place in Pennsylvania. These include <a href="/wiki/Musikfest" title="Musikfest">Musikfest</a> and <a href="/wiki/NEARfest" title="NEARfest">NEARfest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem,_Pennsylvania" title="Bethlehem, Pennsylvania">Bethlehem</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Folk_Festival" title="Philadelphia Folk Festival">Philadelphia Folk Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Creation_Festival" title="Creation Festival">Creation Festival</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Allentown_Fair" title="Great Allentown Fair">Great Allentown Fair</a>, and Purple Door.</p>
<p>There are nearly one million licensed hunters in Pennsylvania. Whitetail deer, black bear, cottontail rabbits, squirrel, turkey, and grouse are common game species. Pennsylvania is considered one of the finest wild turkey hunting states in the Union, alongside Texas and <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>. Sport hunting in Pennsylvania provides a massive boost for the Commonwealth's economy. A report from The Center for Rural Pennsylvania (a Legislative Agency of the Pennsylvania General Assembly) reported that hunting, fishing, and furtaking generated a total of $9.6 billion statewide.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Boone_and_Crockett_Club" title="Boone and Crockett Club">Boone and Crockett Club</a> shows that five of the ten largest (skull size) <a href="/wiki/American_black_bear" title="American black bear">black bear</a> entries came from the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blackbear_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-blackbear-152">[152]</a></sup> The state also has a tied record for the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter" title="Hunter">hunter</a> shot black bear in the Boone &amp; Crockett books at 733 lb (332 kg) and a <a href="/wiki/Skull" title="Skull">skull</a> of 23 3/16 tied with a bear shot in California in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blackbear_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-blackbear-152">[152]</a></sup> The largest bear ever found dead was in <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> in 1975, and the second-largest was shot by a <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poacher</a> in the state in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blackbear_152-2"><a href="#cite_note-blackbear-152">[152]</a></sup> Pennsylvania holds the second-highest number of Boone &amp; Crockett-recorded record black bears at 183, second only to <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>'s 299.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blackbear_152-3"><a href="#cite_note-blackbear-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National-atlas-pennsylvania.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="762" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/National-atlas-pennsylvania.png/210px-National-atlas-pennsylvania.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/National-atlas-pennsylvania.png/315px-National-atlas-pennsylvania.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/National-atlas-pennsylvania.png/420px-National-atlas-pennsylvania.png 2x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National-atlas-pennsylvania.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Pennsylvania, showing major cities and roads</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Pennsylvania" title="List of airports in Pennsylvania">List of airports in Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_transit_authorities_in_Pennsylvania" title="List of public transit authorities in Pennsylvania">List of public transit authorities in Pennsylvania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pennsylvania_railroads" title="List of Pennsylvania railroads">List of Pennsylvania railroads</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:180px;max-width:180px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1650" data-file-width="2272" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel.JPG/178px-Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel.JPG/267px-Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel.JPG/356px-Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel.JPG 2x" width="178"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Exterior</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:180px;max-width:180px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2215_-_Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Tunnel.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/2215_-_Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Tunnel.JPG/178px-2215_-_Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Tunnel.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/2215_-_Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Tunnel.JPG/267px-2215_-_Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Tunnel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/2215_-_Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Tunnel.JPG/356px-2215_-_Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Tunnel.JPG 2x" width="178"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Interior</div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Mountain_Tunnel" title="Allegheny Mountain Tunnel">Allegheny Mountain Tunnel</a> is the longest of the five tunnels on the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Turnpike" title="Pennsylvania Turnpike">Pennsylvania Turnpike</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Department_of_Transportation" title="Pennsylvania Department of Transportation">Pennsylvania Department of Transportation</a>, abbreviated as PennDOT, owns 39,861 miles (64,150 km) of the 121,770 miles (195,970 km) of roadway in the state, making it the fifth-largest state highway system in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennDOT_fact_7_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-PennDOT_fact_7-153">[153]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Turnpike" title="Pennsylvania Turnpike">Pennsylvania Turnpike</a> system is 535 miles (861 km) long, with the mainline portion stretching from Ohio to Philadelphia and New Jersey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennDOT_fact_7_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-PennDOT_fact_7-153">[153]</a></sup> It is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Turnpike_Commission" title="Pennsylvania Turnpike Commission">Pennsylvania Turnpike Commission</a>. Another major east–west route is <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80_in_Pennsylvania" title="Interstate 80 in Pennsylvania">Interstate 80</a>, which runs primarily in the northern tier of the state from Ohio to New Jersey at the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Water_Gap" title="Delaware Water Gap">Delaware Water Gap</a>. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_90_in_Pennsylvania" title="Interstate 90 in Pennsylvania">Interstate 90</a> travels the relatively short distance between Ohio and New York through <a href="/wiki/Erie_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie County, Pennsylvania">Erie County</a>, in the extreme northwestern part of the state.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Appalachian_Throughway.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1661" data-file-width="2718" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Appalachian_Throughway.jpg/210px-Appalachian_Throughway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Appalachian_Throughway.jpg/315px-Appalachian_Throughway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Appalachian_Throughway.jpg/420px-Appalachian_Throughway.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Appalachian_Throughway.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_220" title="U.S. Route 220">U.S. Route 220</a> as it passes through <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Township,_Clinton_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Lamar Township, Clinton County, Pennsylvania">Lamar Township</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Primary north–south highways are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_79_in_Pennsylvania" title="Interstate 79 in Pennsylvania">Interstate 79</a> from its terminus in Erie through Pittsburgh to West Virginia, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_81_in_Pennsylvania" title="Interstate 81 in Pennsylvania">Interstate 81</a> from New York through <a href="/wiki/Scranton,_Pennsylvania" title="Scranton, Pennsylvania">Scranton, Lackawanna County</a> and Harrisburg to Maryland and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_476" title="Interstate 476">Interstate 476</a>, which begins 7 miles (11 km) north of the <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> border, in <a href="/wiki/Chester,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester, Pennsylvania">Chester, Delaware County</a> and travels 132 miles (212 km) to <a href="/wiki/Clarks_Summit,_Pennsylvania" title="Clarks Summit, Pennsylvania">Clarks Summit, Lackawanna County</a>, where it joins I-81. All but 20 miles (32 km) of I-476 is the Northeast Extension of the Pennsylvania Turnpike, while the highway south of the main line of the Pennsylvania Turnpike is officially called the "Veterans Memorial Highway", but is commonly referred to by locals as the "Blue Route".</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/SEPTA" title="SEPTA">Southeastern Pennsylvania Transportation Authority</a> (SEPTA) is the sixth-largest transit agency in the United States and operates the <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavy_rail" title="Heavy rail">heavy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> transit, and <a href="/wiki/Transit_bus" title="Transit bus">transit bus</a> service in the Philadelphia metropolitan area. The <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_Allegheny_County" title="Port Authority of Allegheny County">Port Authority of Allegheny County</a> is the 25th-largest transit agency and provides transit bus and light rail service in and around Pittsburgh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>Intercity passenger rail transit is provided by <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>, with the majority of traffic occurring on the <i><a href="/wiki/Keystone_Service" title="Keystone Service">Keystone Service</a></i> in the high-speed <a href="/wiki/Keystone_Corridor" title="Keystone Corridor">Keystone Corridor</a> between Harrisburg and Philadelphia's <a href="/wiki/30th_Street_Station" title="30th Street Station">30th Street Station</a> before heading north to New York City, as well as the <i><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Northeast Regional</a></i> providing frequent high speed service up and down the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a>. the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pennsylvanian_(Amtrak)" title="Pennsylvanian (Amtrak)">Pennsylvanian</a></i> follows the same route from New York City to Harrisburg, but extends out to Pittsburgh. The <i><a href="/wiki/Capitol_Limited_(Amtrak_train)" title="Capitol Limited (Amtrak train)">Capitol Limited</a></i> also passes through Pittsburgh, as well as <a href="/wiki/Connellsville,_Pennsylvania" title="Connellsville, Pennsylvania">Connellsville</a>, on its way from Chicago to <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennDOT_fact_10_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-PennDOT_fact_10-155">[155]</a></sup> Traveling between Chicago and New York City, the <i><a href="/wiki/Lake_Shore_Limited" title="Lake Shore Limited">Lake Shore Limited</a></i> passes through Erie once in each direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennDOT_fact_10_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-PennDOT_fact_10-155">[155]</a></sup> There are 67 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short-line_railroad" title="Short-line railroad">short-line</a>, freight railroads operating in Pennsylvania, the highest number in any U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennDOT_fact_10_155-2"><a href="#cite_note-PennDOT_fact_10-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pennsylvania has seven major airports: <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">Philadelphia International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_International_Airport" title="Pittsburgh International Airport">Pittsburgh International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley_International_Airport" title="Lehigh Valley International Airport">Lehigh Valley International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg_International_Airport" title="Harrisburg International Airport">Harrisburg International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erie_International_Airport" title="Erie International Airport">Erie International</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_Park_Airport" title="University Park Airport">University Park Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilkes-Barre/Scranton_International_Airport" title="Wilkes-Barre/Scranton International Airport">Wilkes-Barre/Scranton International</a>. A total of 134 public-use airports are located in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PennDOT_fact_10_155-3"><a href="#cite_note-PennDOT_fact_10-155">[155]</a></sup> The port of Pittsburgh is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Inland_port" title="Inland port">inland port</a> in the United States and the 18th-largest port overall; the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Philadelphia" title="Port of Philadelphia">Port of Philadelphia</a> is the 24th-largest port in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Pennsylvania's only port on the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> is located in Erie.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allegheny_River_Lock_and_Dam_Two" title="Allegheny River Lock and Dam Two">Allegheny River Lock and Dam Two</a> is the most-used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lock_(water_transport)" title="Lock (water transport)">lock</a> operated by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">United States Army Corps of Engineers</a> of its 255 nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The dam impounds the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a> near <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">Downtown Pittsburgh</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Pennsylvania" title="Sports in Pennsylvania">Sports in Pennsylvania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citizens_Bank_Park,_May_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1080" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg/220px-Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg/330px-Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg/440px-Citizens_Bank_Park%2C_May_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citizens_Bank_Park,_May_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Citizens_Bank_Park" title="Citizens Bank Park">Citizens Bank Park</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="South Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">South Philadelphia</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pennsylvania is home to many major league professional sports teams; the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers" title="Philadelphia 76ers">Philadelphia 76ers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Philadelphia Flyers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Penguins" title="Pittsburgh Penguins">Pittsburgh Penguins</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Union" title="Philadelphia Union">Philadelphia Union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>. Among them, these teams have accumulated 7 <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> Championships (Pirates 5, Phillies 2), 16 <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> Pennants (Pirates 9, Phillies 7), 3 pre-<a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> era NFL Championships (Eagles), 6 Super Bowl Championships (Steelers), 2 NBA Championships (76ers), and 7 <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cups</a> (Penguins 5, Flyers 2).</p>
<p>Pennsylvania also has minor league and semi-pro sports teams: the <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">Triple-A</a> baseball <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley_IronPigs" title="Lehigh Valley IronPigs">Lehigh Valley IronPigs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scranton/Wilkes-Barre_RailRiders" title="Scranton/Wilkes-Barre RailRiders">Scranton/Wilkes-Barre RailRiders</a> of the <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">International League</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Double-A_(baseball)" title="Double-A (baseball)">Double-A</a> baseball <a href="/wiki/Altoona_Curve" title="Altoona Curve">Altoona Curve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erie_SeaWolves" title="Erie SeaWolves">Erie SeaWolves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg_Senators" title="Harrisburg Senators">Harrisburg Senators</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reading_Fightin_Phils" title="Reading Fightin Phils">Reading Fightin Phils</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_League_(baseball)" title="Eastern League (baseball)">Eastern League</a>; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_A-Short_Season" title="Class A-Short Season">Class A-Short Season</a> baseball <a href="/wiki/State_College_Spikes" title="State College Spikes">State College Spikes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Williamsport_Crosscutters" title="Williamsport Crosscutters">Williamsport Crosscutters</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_York%E2%80%93Penn_League" title="New York–Penn League">New York–Penn League</a>; the independent baseball <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_Barnstormers" title="Lancaster Barnstormers">Lancaster Barnstormers</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_Revolution" title="York Revolution">York Revolution</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_League_of_Professional_Baseball" title="Atlantic League of Professional Baseball">Atlantic League of Professional Baseball</a>; the independent baseball <a href="/wiki/Washington_Wild_Things" title="Washington Wild Things">Washington Wild Things</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Frontier_League" title="Frontier League">Frontier League</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Erie_BayHawks_(2017%E2%80%93)" title="Erie BayHawks (2017–)">Erie BayHawks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/NBA_G_League" title="NBA G League">NBA G League</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley_Phantoms" title="Lehigh Valley Phantoms">Lehigh Valley Phantoms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilkes-Barre/Scranton_Penguins" title="Wilkes-Barre/Scranton Penguins">Wilkes-Barre/Scranton Penguins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hershey_Bears" title="Hershey Bears">Hershey Bears</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">American Hockey League</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Reading_Royals" title="Reading Royals">Reading Royals</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/ECHL" title="ECHL">ECHL</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Soul" title="Philadelphia Soul">Philadelphia Soul</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arena_Football_League" title="Arena Football League">Arena Football League</a>. Among them, these teams have accumulated 12 triple and double A baseball league titles (RailRiders 1, Senators 6, Fightin Phils 4 Curve 1), 1 Arena Bowl Championship (Soul), and 11 <a href="/wiki/Calder_Cup" title="Calder Cup">Calder Cups</a> (Bears).</p>
<p>Since 1959, the <a href="/wiki/Little_League_World_Series" title="Little League World Series">Little League World Series</a> is held each summer in <a href="/wiki/South_Williamsport,_Pennsylvania" title="South Williamsport, Pennsylvania">South Williamsport</a>, near where <a href="/wiki/Little_League_Baseball" title="Little League Baseball">Little League Baseball</a> was founded in <a href="/wiki/Williamsport,_Pennsylvania" title="Williamsport, Pennsylvania">Williamsport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LittleLeagueChronology_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-LittleLeagueChronology-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also, the first World Series between the Boston Pilgrims (which became the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> was played in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> in 1903.</p>
<p>Soccer is gaining popularity within the state of Pennsylvania as well. With the addition of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Union" title="Philadelphia Union">Philadelphia Union</a> in the MLS, the state now boasts three teams that are eligible to compete for the <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Hunt_U.S._Open_Cup" title="Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup">Lamar Hunt U.S. Open Cup</a> annually. The other two teams are the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Riverhounds" title="Pittsburgh Riverhounds">Pittsburgh Riverhounds</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg_City_Islanders" title="Harrisburg City Islanders">Harrisburg City Islanders</a>, both of the United Soccer Leagues Second Division (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USL-2" title="USL-2">USL-2</a>). Within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Soccer_Pyramid" title="American Soccer Pyramid">American Soccer Pyramid</a>, the MLS takes the first tier, while the USL-2 claims the third tier.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG/220px-Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG/330px-Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG/440px-Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pocono_Victory_Lane.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> racing at <a href="/wiki/Pocono_Raceway" title="Pocono Raceway">Pocono Raceway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Long_Pond,_Pennsylvania" title="Long Pond, Pennsylvania">Long Pond</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In motorsports, the <a href="/wiki/Mario_Andretti" title="Mario Andretti">Mario Andretti</a> dynasty of race drivers hails from <a href="/wiki/Nazareth,_Pennsylvania" title="Nazareth, Pennsylvania">Nazareth</a> in the Lehigh Valley. Notable racetracks in Pennsylvania include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jennerstown_Speedway" title="Jennerstown Speedway">Jennerstown Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jennerstown,_Pennsylvania" title="Jennerstown, Pennsylvania">Jennerstown</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie_Speedway" title="Lake Erie Speedway">Lake Erie Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_East,_Pennsylvania" title="North East, Pennsylvania">North East</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mahoning_Valley_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mahoning Valley Speedway (page does not exist)">Mahoning Valley Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lehighton,_Pennsylvania" title="Lehighton, Pennsylvania">Lehighton</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Motordome_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Motordome Speedway (page does not exist)">Motordome Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Smithton,_Pennsylvania" title="Smithton, Pennsylvania">Smithton</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mountain_Speedway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mountain Speedway (page does not exist)">Mountain Speedway</a> in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=St._Johns,_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="St. Johns, Pennsylvania (page does not exist)">St. Johns</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nazareth_Speedway" title="Nazareth Speedway">Nazareth Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nazareth,_Pennsylvania" title="Nazareth, Pennsylvania">Nazareth</a> (closed); and the <a href="/wiki/Pocono_Raceway" title="Pocono Raceway">Pocono Raceway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Long_Pond,_Pennsylvania" title="Long Pond, Pennsylvania">Long Pond</a>, which is home to two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASCAR_Cup_Series" title="NASCAR Cup Series">NASCAR Cup Series</a> races and an <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a> race. The state is also home to Maple Grove Raceway, near Reading, which hosts major <a href="/wiki/National_Hot_Rod_Association" title="National Hot Rod Association">National Hot Rod Association</a> sanctioned drag racing events each year.</p>
<p>There are also two <a href="/wiki/Motocross" title="Motocross">motocross</a> race tracks that host a round of the AMA Toyota Motocross Championships in Pennsylvania. <a class="external text" href="http://www.highpointmx.com/" rel="nofollow">High Point Raceway</a> in located in Mt. Morris, Pennsylvania, and Steel City is located in Delmont, Pennsylvania.</p>
<p>Horse racing courses in Pennsylvania consist of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Meadows_Racetrack" title="The Meadows Racetrack">The Meadows</a> near Pittsburgh, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pocono_Downs" title="Pocono Downs">Pocono Downs</a> in Wilkes-Barre, and <a href="/wiki/Harrah%27s_Philadelphia" title="Harrah's Philadelphia">Harrah's Philadelphia</a> in Chester, which offer <a href="/wiki/Harness_racing" title="Harness racing">harness racing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Penn_National_Race_Course" title="Penn National Race Course">Penn National Race Course</a> in <a href="/wiki/Grantville,_Pennsylvania" title="Grantville, Pennsylvania">Grantville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parx_Casino_and_Racing" title="Parx Casino and Racing">Parx Racing</a> (formerly Philadelphia Park) in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bensalem,_Pennsylvania" title="Bensalem, Pennsylvania">Bensalem</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Presque_Isle_Downs" title="Presque Isle Downs">Presque Isle Downs</a> near Erie, which offer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_racing" title="Thoroughbred racing">thoroughbred racing</a>. <a href="/wiki/Smarty_Jones" title="Smarty Jones">Smarty Jones</a>, the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Derby" title="Kentucky Derby">Kentucky Derby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Preakness_Stakes" title="Preakness Stakes">Preakness Stakes</a> winner, had Philadelphia Park as his home course.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arnold_Palmer" title="Arnold Palmer">Arnold Palmer</a>, one of the 20th century's most notable pro golfers, comes from <a href="/wiki/Latrobe,_Pennsylvania" title="Latrobe, Pennsylvania">Latrobe</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Jim_Furyk" title="Jim Furyk">Jim Furyk</a>, a current <a href="/wiki/Professional_Golfers%27_Association_of_America" title="Professional Golfers' Association of America">PGA</a> member, grew up near in <a href="/wiki/Manheim_Township,_Lancaster_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Manheim Township, Lancaster County, Pennsylvania">Lancaster</a>. PGA tournaments in Pennsylvania include the 84 Lumber Classic, played at Nemacolin Woodlands Resort, in <a href="/wiki/Farmington,_Pennsylvania" title="Farmington, Pennsylvania">Farmington</a> and the Northeast Pennsylvania Classic, played at Glenmaura National Golf Club, in <a href="/wiki/Moosic,_Pennsylvania" title="Moosic, Pennsylvania">Moosic</a>.</p>
<p>Philadelphia is home to <a href="/wiki/LOVE_Park" title="LOVE Park">LOVE Park</a>, once a popular spot for <a href="/wiki/Skateboard" title="Skateboard">skateboarding</a>, and across from City Hall, host to <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>'s <a href="/wiki/X_Games" title="X Games">X Games</a> in 2001 and 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="College_sports">College sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: College sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>College football is popular in Pennsylvania<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. There are three colleges in Pennsylvania that play at the highest level of collegiate football competition, the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision">NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision</a>. Two play in <a href="/wiki/Power_Five_conferences" title="Power Five conferences">Power Five conferences</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penn_State_University" title="Penn State University">Penn State University</a> <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Nittany_Lions_football" title="Penn State Nittany Lions football">Nittany Lions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a> <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">Panthers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple University</a> <a href="/wiki/Temple_Owls_football" title="Temple Owls football">Owls</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American Athletic Conference</a>. Penn State, claims two <a href="/wiki/College_football_national_championships_in_NCAA_Division_I_FBS" title="College football national championships in NCAA Division I FBS">national championships</a> (1982 &amp; 1986) as well as seven undefeated seasons (1887, 1912, 1968, 1969, 1973, 1986 and 1994). Penn State plays its home games in the second-largest stadium in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Beaver_Stadium" title="Beaver Stadium">Beaver Stadium</a>, which seats 107,282, and is currently led by head coach <a href="/wiki/James_Franklin_(American_football_coach)" title="James Franklin (American football coach)">James Franklin</a>. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitt_Panthers" title="Pitt Panthers">Panthers</a> claims nine national championships (1915, 1916, 1918, 1929, 1931, 1934, 1936, 1937 and 1976) and has played eight undefeated seasons (1904, 1910, 1915, 1916, 1917, 1920, 1937 and 1976).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Pitt plays its home games at <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a>, a facility it shares with the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a>, and is led by current head football coach <a href="/wiki/Pat_Narduzzi" title="Pat Narduzzi">Pat Narduzzi</a>. Other Pennsylvania schools that have won national titles in football include <a href="/wiki/Lafayette_College" title="Lafayette College">Lafayette College</a> (1896), Villanova University (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I Football Championship">FCS</a> 2009), the <a href="/wiki/Penn_Quakers_football" title="Penn Quakers football">University of Pennsylvania</a> (1895, 1897, 1904 and 1908)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> and Washington and Jefferson College (1921).</p>
<p>College basketball is also popular in the state, especially in the Philadelphia area where five universities, collectively termed the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Big_5" title="Philadelphia Big 5">Big Five</a>, have a rich tradition in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> basketball. National titles in college basketball have been won by the following Pennsylvania universities: <a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University" title="La Salle University">La Salle University</a> (1954), <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple University</a> (1938), <a href="/wiki/Penn_Quakers_men%27s_basketball" title="Penn Quakers men's basketball">University of Pennsylvania</a> (1920 and 1921), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a> (1928 and 1930), and <a href="/wiki/Villanova_University" title="Villanova University">Villanova University</a> (1985 and 2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1532" data-file-width="2071" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg/220px-Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg/330px-Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg/440px-Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hershey_Pennsylvania_1976.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/The_Hershey_Company" title="The Hershey Company">Hershey Chocolate Factory</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In his book <i>Yo Mama Cooks Like a Yankee</i>, author Sharon Hernes Silverman calls Pennsylvania the snack food capital of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> It leads all other states in the manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Pretzel" title="Pretzel">pretzels</a> and potato chips. The <a href="/wiki/Sturgis_Pretzel_House" title="Sturgis Pretzel House">Sturgis Pretzel House</a> introduced the pretzel to America, and companies like Anderson Bakery Company, Intercourse Pretzel Factory, and <a href="/wiki/Snyder%27s_of_Hanover" title="Snyder's of Hanover">Snyder's of Hanover</a> are leading manufacturers in the Commonwealth. Two of the three companies that define the U.S. potato chip industry are based in Pennsylvania: <a href="/wiki/Utz_Quality_Foods" title="Utz Quality Foods">Utz Quality Foods</a>, which started making chips in <a href="/wiki/Hanover,_Pennsylvania" title="Hanover, Pennsylvania">Hanover, Pennsylvania</a> in 1921, and <a href="/wiki/Wise_Foods" title="Wise Foods">Wise Foods</a> which started making chips in <a href="/wiki/Berwick,_Pennsylvania" title="Berwick, Pennsylvania">Berwick</a> in 1921 (the third, <a href="/wiki/Frito-Lay" title="Frito-Lay">Lay's Potato Chips</a>, is a Texas company). Other companies such as <a href="/wiki/Herr%27s_Snacks" title="Herr's Snacks">Herr's Snacks</a>, Martin's Potato Chips, Snyder's of Berlin (not associated with Snyder's of Hanover) and Troyer Farms Potato Products are popular chip manufacturers.</p>
<p>The U.S. chocolate industry is centered in <a href="/wiki/Hershey,_Pennsylvania" title="Hershey, Pennsylvania">Hershey, Pennsylvania</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Mars,_Incorporated" title="Mars, Incorporated">Mars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Godiva_Chocolatier" title="Godiva Chocolatier">Godiva</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wilbur_Chocolate_Company" title="Wilbur Chocolate Company">Wilbur Chocolate Company</a> nearby, and smaller manufacturers such as Asher's<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Souderton,_Pennsylvania" title="Souderton, Pennsylvania">Souderton</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Hawk_Chocolates" title="Gertrude Hawk Chocolates">Gertrude Hawk Chocolates</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dunmore,_Pennsylvania" title="Dunmore, Pennsylvania">Dunmore</a>. Other notable companies include <a href="/wiki/Just_Born" title="Just Born">Just Born</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem,_Pennsylvania" title="Bethlehem, Pennsylvania">Bethlehem, Pennsylvania</a>, makers of <a href="/wiki/Hot_Tamales" title="Hot Tamales">Hot Tamales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_and_Ike" title="Mike and Ike">Mike and Ikes</a>, the Easter favorite marshmallow <a href="/wiki/Peeps" title="Peeps">Peeps</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boyer_Brothers" title="Boyer Brothers">Boyer Brothers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Altoona,_Pennsylvania" title="Altoona, Pennsylvania">Altoona, Pennsylvania</a>, which is well known for its Mallo Cups. <a href="/wiki/Auntie_Anne%27s" title="Auntie Anne's">Auntie Anne's Pretzels</a> began as a market-stand in Downingtown, Pennsylvania, and now has corporate headquarters in Lancaster City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Traditional Pennsylvania Dutch foods include chicken potpie, ham potpie, schnitz un knepp (dried apples, ham, and dumplings), <a href="/wiki/Fasnacht_(doughnut)" title="Fasnacht (doughnut)">fasnachts</a> (raised doughnuts), scrapple, pretzels, bologna, chow-chow, and <a href="/wiki/Shoofly_pie" title="Shoofly pie">Shoofly pie</a>. <a href="/wiki/Martin%27s_Famous_Pastry_Shoppe,_Inc." title="Martin's Famous Pastry Shoppe, Inc.">Martin's Famous Pastry Shoppe, Inc.</a>, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Chambersburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Chambersburg, Pennsylvania">Chambersburg, Pennsylvania</a>, specializes in potato bread, another <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Pennsylvania_Dutch" title="Cuisine of the Pennsylvania Dutch">traditional Pennsylvania Dutch food</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D.G._Yuengling_%26_Son" title="D.G. Yuengling &amp; Son">D.G. Yuengling &amp; Son</a>, America's oldest brewery, has been brewing beer in <a href="/wiki/Pottsville,_Pennsylvania" title="Pottsville, Pennsylvania">Pottsville</a> since 1829.</p>
<p>Among the regional foods associated with Philadelphia are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheesesteaks" title="Cheesesteaks">cheesesteaks</a>, hoagie, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soft_pretzels" title="Soft pretzels">soft pretzels</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_water_ice" title="Italian water ice">Italian water ice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_potato_candy" title="Irish potato candy">Irish potato candy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scrapple" title="Scrapple">scrapple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tastykake" title="Tastykake">Tastykake</a>, Wawa, and <a href="/wiki/Stromboli_(food)" title="Stromboli (food)">strombolis</a>. In Pittsburgh, tomato ketchup was improved by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H._J._Heinz_Company" title="H. J. Heinz Company">Henry John Heinz</a> from 1876 to the early 20th century. Famous to a lesser extent than Heinz ketchup are the Pittsburgh's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primanti_Brothers_Restaurant" title="Primanti Brothers Restaurant">Primanti Brothers Restaurant</a> sandwiches, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pierogies" title="Pierogies">pierogies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/City_chicken" title="City chicken">city chicken</a>. Outside of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scranton" title="Scranton">Scranton</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Old_Forge,_Lackawanna_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Old Forge, Lackawanna County, Pennsylvania">Old Forge</a> there are dozens of Italian restaurants specializing in pizza made unique by thick, light crust and American cheese. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erie" title="Erie">Erie</a> also has its share of unique foods, including Greek sauce and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sponge_candy" title="Sponge candy">sponge candy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">Sauerkraut</a> along with pork and mashed potatoes is a common meal on New Year's Day in Pennsylvania.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nicknames">Nicknames</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Nicknames">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Pennsylvania has been known as the <a href="/wiki/Keystone_(architecture)" title="Keystone (architecture)"><i>Keystone</i></a> <i>State</i> since 1802,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-171">[171]</a></sup> based in part upon its central location among the original <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> forming the United States, and also in part because of the number of important American documents signed in the state (such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>). It was also a keystone state economically, having both the industry common to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">North</a> (making such wares as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conestoga_wagons" title="Conestoga wagons">Conestoga wagons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_rifle" title="Long rifle">rifles</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> and the agriculture common to the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a> (producing feed, fiber, food, and tobacco).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another one of Pennsylvania's nicknames is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_Society_of_Friends" title="Religious Society of Friends"><i>Quaker</i></a> <i>State</i>; in colonial times, it was known officially as the <i><a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">Quaker Province</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> in recognition of Quaker<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Frame_of_Government_of_Pennsylvania" title="Frame of Government of Pennsylvania">First Frame of Government</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> constitution for Pennsylvania that guaranteed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_(political)" title="Freedom (political)">liberty</a> of <a href="/wiki/Conscience" title="Conscience">conscience</a>. He knew of the hostility<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Quakers faced when they opposed religious ritual, taking oaths, violence, war and military service, and what they viewed as ostentatious <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/frippery" title="wikt:frippery">frippery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<b>The Coal State</b>", "<b>The Oil State</b>", "<b>The Chocolate State</b>", and "<b>The Steel State</b>" were adopted when those were the state's greatest industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>"The State of Independence" currently appears on many road signs entering the state.</p>

<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://avalon.law.yale.edu/17th_century/pa01.asp" rel="nofollow">Charter for the Province of Pennsylvania-1681</a>. This charter, granted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_II_(England)" title="Charles II (England)">Charles II (England)</a> to William Penn, constituted him and his heirs proprietors of the province, which, in honor of his father, <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">Admiral</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Penn_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="William Penn (Royal Navy officer)">William Penn</a>, (whose cash advances and services were thus requited,) was called Pennsylvania. To perfect his title, <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a> purchased, on 1682-08-24, a quit-claim from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_II_(England)" title="James II (England)">Duke of York</a> to the lands west of the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a> embraced in his patent of 1664</span></li>
